# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Scheduler Binding to kubelet Pod Admission Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a scheduler binding decision reaches the kubelet in kubernetes/kubernetes. Find Go source files implementing: the scheduler Bind call, the API server binding handler, the kubelet pod watch/sync, and the pod admission gates that decide whether to start a bound pod.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],

  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I have successfully completed the task. The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json` and contains a comprehensive trace of how a scheduler binding decision reaches the kubelet through the Kubernetes architecture.

## Summary

I traced the complete flow from scheduler binding decision to kubelet pod admission:

1. **Scheduler Binding Call** (`pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:bindingCycle` → `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/defaultbinder/default_binder.go:Bind`)
   - The scheduler's binding cycle invokes the DefaultBinder plugin
   - The Bind method creates a Binding object and calls the Kubernetes API client

2. **API Server Binding Handler** (`pkg/registry/core/pod/storage/storage.go:BindingREST`)
   - The `Create()` method validates and processes the binding request
   - `assignPod()` and `setPodHostAndAnnotations()` update the pod's `spec.nodeName` in etcd
   - Sets the `PodScheduled` condition to indicate the pod is bound

3. **Kubelet Pod Discovery** (`pkg/kubelet/config/apiserver.go:NewSourceApiserver`)
   - Creates a field selector to watch pods where `spec.nodeName` matches the kubelet's node
   - Uses a Reflector to synchronize pod updates from the API server
   - Sends pod updates through the kubelet's configuration channel

4. **Pod Admission Gates** (`pkg/kubelet/lifecycle/interfaces.go` and `predicate.go`)
   - Defines `PodAdmitHandler` interface and `PodAdmitAttributes` for admission checks
   - `predicateAdmitHandler` validates resource availability, OS compatibility, and constraints
   - The `canAdmitPod()` method in kubelet.go iterates through registered handlers

5. **Pod Synchronization** (`pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go:SyncPod`)
   - Called after pod admission succeeds
   - Orchestrates container creation, volume mounting, and networking
   
... (truncated)

Scheduler Bind Plugin (pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/defaultbinder/default_binder.go)\\nThe `DefaultBinder` plugin implements the `BindPlugin` interface and executes the actual binding. Scheduler Bind Plugin (pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/defaultbinder/default_binder.go)\\nThe `DefaultBinder` plugin implements the `BindPlugin` interface and executes the actual binding. Kubelet Pod Discovery from API Server (pkg/kubelet/config/apiserver.go)\\nOnce a pod is bound to a node, the kubelet discovers it through the API server source:\\n- `NewSourceApiserver()` (lines 37-54) creates a field selector for pods matching the node's name\\n- It uses a `ListWatcher` to watch pods where `spec.nodeName` matches the kubelet's node\\n- `newSourceApiserverFromLW()` (lines 57-68) creates a `Reflector` that watches the API server and sends `PodUpdate` events to the kubelet's config channel\\n- Updates are sent with operation type `kubetypes.SET` to the kubelet's pod config system\\n\\n### 5. Pod Admission in Kubelet (pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go)\\nThe kubelet's `canAdmitPod()` method (lines 2348-2352):\\n- Retrieves all currently allocated pods on the node\\n- Creates `PodAdmitAttributes` with the pod being evaluated and other pods\\n- Iterates through registered `admitHandlers` (line 2355)\\n- Returns false if any handler rejects the pod, preventing it from being started\\n\\n### 7. Pod Synchronization (pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go)\\nOnce a pod is admitted, the kubelet's `SyncPod()` method (lines 1844-1848):\\n- Receives the pod from the config system\\n- Orchestrates container creation, volume mounting, and networking\\n- Manages the pod's lifecycle through to completion\\n\\n### Complete Flow Summary\\nThe chain flows as follows:\\n1. Scheduler's `bindingCycle()` calls `DefaultBinder.Bind()`\\n2. Binder makes REST call to API server: `Pods.Bind(binding)`\\n3. API server's `BindingREST.Create()` updates pod with `spec.nodeName`\\n4. Kubelet's API server watcher detects the bound pod via `NewSourceApiserver()` reflector\\n5. Pod is passed to `canAdmitPod()` which runs `PodAdmitHandler` gates\\n6. If admitted, `SyncPod()` is called to manage the pod's runtime lifecycle\\n\\nThis architecture ensures that scheduler decisions are properly propagated to the kubelet through the API server, with intermediate admission checks at the kubelet level to guarantee the pod can actually run on the node before containers are started.\"\n}\n",
